<div id="review_1423457887" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1423457887" />
    <a title="XLXL" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48198151-xlxl"><img alt="XLXL" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1423457887?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="XLXL" class="user" itemprop="url" name="XLXL" href="/user/show/48198151-xlxl">XLXL</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1423457887" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1399983582385657413">Enough has been said here about the plot summary and I don't want to repeat again. This is more than a Sci-Fi story and its freshness shocks me.<br/><br/>The author definitely has a genius imagination but it is the scientific ideas that backs up and moves the story. Many sci-fi stories nowadays are more fantasy than science fiction. Taken out a few galactic battles, those stories around things like empire, rebellion and senate fall back directly to ancient Roman times or Middle Earth. Instead of forward l</span>
  <span id="freeText1399983582385657413" style="display:none">Enough has been said here about the plot summary and I don't want to repeat again. This is more than a Sci-Fi story and its freshness shocks me.<br /><br />The author definitely has a genius imagination but it is the scientific ideas that backs up and moves the story. Many sci-fi stories nowadays are more fantasy than science fiction. Taken out a few galactic battles, those stories around things like empire, rebellion and senate fall back directly to ancient Roman times or Middle Earth. Instead of forward looking, those are just images of past in our mind. Not this book. Without its shining ideas based on science, the whole plot just won't stand up. Yet the author explains the science bit so well that an average non science reader like me can understand. In this aspect the book really belongs to the same league of the golden age Sci-Fi, when fast scientific development made Sci-Fi masters wonder what ifs.<br /><br />The book bases its plot on a unique theme: what if earth came across a far advanced civilization that has to annihilate us. Over the years, there are thousands of aliens in Sci-Fi. They are either advanced both technically AND morally, or have some laughable weakness that gives human an easy win. In Avatar, earth is so advanced that we go out to colonize. It's quite uncommon that a book explores what if our technology is like bugs compared with that of alien who doesn't even care what we've got. Many readers puzzled at the level of despair and the extreme social reactions in the book, which is extremely rare in Sci-Fi before. However, it shouldn’t sound too strange to many Asian readers including me as our civilization survived a similar encounter with a near alien civilization just 200 years ago.<br /><br />Since the discovery of America and the especially industrial revolution, European civilization annihilated civilizations in two Americas and Australia, segmented Islamic world and fully colonized India. East Asian civilizations escaped the fate and flourished, but not without scars from extreme social movements and widespread despair along the way. There are some common traits in the process. 1st, they all managed to catch up the technology gap. 2nd, the process was organized by a somewhat central organization. 3rd, standing at the centre of violent social process and somewhat a testament to the degree of confrontation, the leaders of that organization all suffered personal tragedies. Japan's escape was pushed mainly by lower ranking samurai. One of the three main leaders was forced to suicide in typical Japanese style (hara-kiri). Another one was assassinated. Japanese people continue on this radical road till met with 2 A bombs. The main force behind South Korean's advance is its undemocratic military junta. Its leader came to power in military coup and ordered the killings of hundreds of demonstrators. Both his wife and himself assassinated. In terms of China, that one organization is CCP and here is a list of personal loss for its leader Mao: Three siblings all died unnaturally. Sister-tortured to death in prison, brother1-died of guerrilla warfare, brother2-poisoned. Three wives in his life.1st -executed in prison, 2nd - mad after losing 6 children during long march and her sister died in car accident decades later in search of the children in an effort to salvage her sister's marriage. 3rd- the red queen, committed suicide following Mao's ideal. Out of 10 children Mao had, two daughters and a mad son survived. 6 were lost during long march except the eldest son, who went to Soviet fighting Germans as a tank officer and was killed in Korean War by US flame bombs. Mao himself, ironically enough, was turned into a symbol and indeed a weapon after death by his comrades who actually betrayed his ideal (he was mummified). The violent modern history of these ancient civilizations across several continents after such an encounter forms the basis of author's imagination on the level of social unrest and the price to pay. If the galaxy does have millions of civilizations, what is waiting for us, especially when we think about the fact that European civilization is only one generation of technology ahead by then and by no means a dark one? What will we choose then? It is this question that enhances the book from a great Sci-Fi story to something meaningful to the whole mankind.<br /><br />Though equally moved by some of his short stories, especially Mountain and Wandering Earth, I think the trilogy is worthy of its near cult status in China. People from various backgrounds are so moved that they made music themselves for it ranging from traditional Peking Opera type to underground rock. Hot debate broke out among fans on if the logic of the book really stands (seriously? for a Sci-Fi novel?). Chinese space agency even consulted the author on certain issues. Now the balance between author's day job as a hydro IT engineer and a quiet Sci-Fi writer after work is broken. It was this balance that gave the author the inspiration years ago to build a computer model to study the interaction of millions of worlds in the universe and the result was shocking. Maybe this is why his narrative sometimes reveals a god like angle, as somewhere in the author's hard disk lies a pocket universe where sagas and heroes rise and fall in a split of second.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1399983582385657413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1751688409" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1751688409" />
    <a title="Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36819318-scott"><img alt="Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485843897p2/36819318.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1751688409?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott" href="/user/show/36819318-scott">Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36819318-scott?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1751688409" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1513303140444917418">Liu Cixin knows how to write a concept novel. The first book in his remembrance of things past trilogy, <i>The Three Body Problem</i>, was based on a fascinating physics model that Liu used to great effect in his story of interstellar first contact and the terrifying ramifications of discovering intelligent life in the universe.<br/><br/>At the heart of <i>The Dark forest</i> is another fascinating concept based on Liu's exploration of the Fermi paradox - the confounding absence of intelligent life in a galaxy that sur</span>
  <span id="freeText1513303140444917418" style="display:none">Liu Cixin knows how to write a concept novel. The first book in his remembrance of things past trilogy, <i>The Three Body Problem</i>, was based on a fascinating physics model that Liu used to great effect in his story of interstellar first contact and the terrifying ramifications of discovering intelligent life in the universe.<br /><br />At the heart of <i>The Dark forest</i> is another fascinating concept based on Liu's exploration of the Fermi paradox - the confounding absence of intelligent life in a galaxy that surely must have other sentient species in it. Other authors (Such as Alistair Reynolds with his Inhibitors in the <i>Revelation Space</i> universe) have dealt with this paradox, but Cixin approaches it from a new and interesting perspective, making this novel more than the sum of its imminent-alien-invasion parts.<br /><br /><i>The Dark forest</i> is a book of two quite different halves, one set in our contemporary world, and another set two centuries away. <br /><br />The setting is one of great tension. After the events of <i>The Three Body Problem</i> a Trisolaran invasion fleet is enroute to Earth, estimated to arrive in approximately four hundred years. Trisolaran technology far outstrips Earth’s and through quantum level spying and sabotage the Trisolarans have crippled humankind’s scientific progression, preventing any further physics research beyond the theories that we have already formulated. <br /><br />A desperate race begins as the world’s powers try to develop weapons, ships, tactics and hibernation technology (To save the brightest minds for future eras when technology has progressed enough to implement their ideas) based on the limited research available, while preventing humanity from succumbing to defeatism in the face of their superior foe.<br /><br />This defeatism is pretty contagious, and justifiably so. Through their quantum agents, known as ‘sophons’ the Trisolarans can spy on anything and anyone on earth. They can read emails, scan computers and listen to conversations. The only place they cannot penetrate is the human mind – the hidden schemes and thoughts of people are safe from their eavesdropping.<br /><br />Knowing this, the governments of the world create a strategic program known as the Wallfacer project, where four individuals are empowered with vast resources and nearly unquestionable authority in order to create war-winning plans that are kept secret inside their own minds. One of these men (and they are, sadly, all men) is a middling academic named Luo Ji, and it is his story that is the primary thread through Cixin’s novel.<br /><br />Ji is eventually hibernated and awoken in a bright technological future where humanity is confident of defeating Trisolaris on the battlefield and has no need for Wallfacers or the Wallfacer project. Ji returns to normal life, but the optimism of the future is not entirely well-founded, and he finds himself being drawn back into the fight with Earth's extraterrestrial enemies.<br /><br />At first, I thought this was going to be an inferior book to <i>The Three Body Problem</i>. The future, semi-utopia section of the book was a touch unconvincing and I didn't quite buy the level of progress humanity had made in two centuries, but as I read on the story drew me in and engaged me with humanity’s struggle and Luo Ji’s personal travails. There were a few chapters where I questioned Cixin's narrative direction, but if you find yourself feeling this way I urge you to trust the author- everything pays off and leads to interesting conclusions. <br /><br />This is a different book from the first in the series, set in what for me was a less interesting setting (I loved the Chinese cultural revolution sections of <i>The Three Body Problem</i>) but it's still an enjoyable, pacey and entertaining novel that reaches a genuinely interesting conclusion. Cixin deftly balances the urgency of facing a genocidal invasion with the creep of despair and complacency over the four-hundred year preparation period and kept me engaged from the first page to the last. <br /><br />If you enjoyed Cixin's first book in this series <i>The Dark forest</i> is well worth your time, and I'm looking forward to the conclusion of this trilogy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1513303140444917418" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2448130090" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2448130090" />
    <a title="ChopinFC" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51633786-chopinfc"><img alt="ChopinFC" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545283749p2/51633786.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2448130090?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ChopinFC" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ChopinFC" href="/user/show/51633786-chopinfc">ChopinFC</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24375664-the-dark-forest">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51633786-chopinfc?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51633786-chopinfc?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51633786-chopinfc?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2448130090" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15087833529113304867"><b>Stunning. Masterpiece. Speechless. </b><br/><br/><br/><i>"Right now, the greatest obstacle to humanity's survival comes from itself."<br/><br/>- Dark Forest </i><br/><br/><b>Liu Xiu’s <i> Dark Forest</i> vastly improves from it’s near perfect predecessor - making my heart pound with tension and excitement!</b> To say that <i>Dark Forest</i> is stunning achievement in the Sci-Fi genre is not an exaggeration! It’s chinese author, Liu Xiu, is able to carry on a story with such clarity and effectiveness that near the last 100 pages I literally though our planet Ear</span>
  <span id="freeText15087833529113304867" style="display:none"><b>Stunning. Masterpiece. Speechless. </b><br><br><br><i>"Right now, the greatest obstacle to humanity's survival comes from itself."<br><br>- Dark Forest </i><br><br><b>Liu Xiu’s <i> Dark Forest</i> vastly improves from it’s near perfect predecessor - making my heart pound with tension and excitement!</b> To say that <i>Dark Forest</i> is stunning achievement in the Sci-Fi genre is not an exaggeration! It’s chinese author, Liu Xiu, is able to carry on a story with such clarity and effectiveness that near the last 100 pages I literally though our planet Earth was about to be invaded by Trisolarans! <br> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555536434i/27377713._SX540_.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <i>Trisolarans vs Earth</i><br><br><br><i>The Three Body Problem</i> carefully carves the foundation for a complex story of Earth’s domination by an alien species. <i> The Dark Forest</i> advances the plot and the story exponentially, by expounding humanity’s response to the threat of Earth’s invasion and ultimate destruction. <b> The end results are astounding!<b></b><br><br><u>Survival</u> is the core thematic emblem within the story.</b> Liu Xiu contrasts the notion of survival of a civilization/species in both iterations, by first giving us the ‘alien perspective’ in <i>The Three Body Problem</i>. In this latest book, readers have the privilege to see humanity’s struggle for survival at at its most basic element! The author strips all pretentions, and portrays humans at their most fragile state! The narrative becomes almost an exposition of the human psyche in face of overwhelmingly grim odds. <br> <br><b><i> Dark Forest</i> is even more ambitious than the first book, as it exposes the readers to humanity in both the present and the future! </b>The juxtaposition between the present and the future fascinated me! Despite the ‘cheesy’ futuristic visions of some sci-fi authors, Liu Xiu is able to craft a future humanity where reality is just a few discoveries away. <u>It’s amazing to see humans in the future adapting their way of life all in name of survival!</u> It's as if human evolution has revolved around the protection of Earth against the impending ‘trisolaran’s invasion! There’ s still a considerable amount of ‘sci-fi’ hardcore elements, but it does not detract from the story- and if anything the science is more intuitive in this second book. <br><br><br><i>Time is the one thing that can’t be stopped. Like a sharp blade, it silently cuts through hard and soft, constantly advancing. Nothing is capable of jolting it even the slightest bit, but it changes everything.”<br><br>- Dark Forest</i><br><br> Liu Xiu does an amazing job at character development, but it is the action and unrelenting <u>tension</u> that build up in the narrative that ultimately makes this a superb read! I shit you not, around the last ⅓ of the book, I could not stop reading the pages!! The tension in the narrative was expressed in so many ways: from the action scenes involving intergalactic battles, or as subtle as a human’s inner emotional struggle to cope with the reality of possible doom. <br><br><br><b> <i> Dark Forest</i> achieves the near impossible task of improving in almost every facet of the first book, and is a perfect example of a sci-fi masterpiece that should be read by all fans of the genre! <br><br><br>5 Stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15087833529113304867" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1368284974" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1368284974" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10743961-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1368284974?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-male">author-male</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1368284974" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15722437341039379569"><b>Executive Summary:</b> I'm not sure what happened. I really enjoyed <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20518872.The_Three_Body_Problem__Three_Body___1_' title='The Three-Body Problem (Three-Body, #1) by Liu Cixin' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Three-Body Problem</a>, but I found myself largely bored by this one.<br/><br/><b>Audio book:</b> I don't like when series change narrators between books. I'm also a huge fan of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2978188.Luke_Daniels' title='Luke Daniels' rel='nofollow noopener'>Luke Daniels</a>, but he wasn't really the best fit for this series. So I was willing to give P. J. Ochlan a chance. I thought he was fine, but he wasn't really any better. It would probably just have been better to stick with Mr. Daniels.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br/>After enjoying <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20518872.The_Three_Body_Problem__Three_Body___1_' title='The Three-Body Problem (Three-Body, #1) by Liu Cixin' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Three-</a></span>
  <span id="freeText15722437341039379569" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> I'm not sure what happened. I really enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20518872.The_Three_Body_Problem__Three_Body___1_" title="The Three-Body Problem (Three-Body, #1) by Liu Cixin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Three-Body Problem</a>, but I found myself largely bored by this one.<br /><br /><b>Audio book:</b> I don't like when series change narrators between books. I'm also a huge fan of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2978188.Luke_Daniels" title="Luke Daniels" rel="nofollow noopener">Luke Daniels</a>, but he wasn't really the best fit for this series. So I was willing to give P. J. Ochlan a chance. I thought he was fine, but he wasn't really any better. It would probably just have been better to stick with Mr. Daniels.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />After enjoying <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20518872.The_Three_Body_Problem__Three_Body___1_" title="The Three-Body Problem (Three-Body, #1) by Liu Cixin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Three-Body Problem</a> a few months ago, I was looking forward to this one. I struggled at the start of that book, but ended up largely enjoying it. I kept waiting for that to happen here, but it never did.<br /><br />The dialogue was hard to listen to. There was far too many times when one character was explaining what another character was doing in EXCRUCIATING detail. I'm not sure if this has more to do with the change in translator, or if I just didn't notice as much in the last book.<br /><br />The characters were pretty bland again, save for the cop again. However, unlike the last book the story and the science were enough to make up for that to me.<br /><br />I thought the end of the book was interesting, and it peaked my curiousity about what happens in the final book, but I think it's too little too late.<br /><br />Overall, I was pretty disappointed, and doubt I'll bother with the last book when it comes out.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15706770075096526421">An incredibly epic science fiction novel! Highly recommended. The scope is amazing. <br/><br/>A different style from the more 'grounded' Three Body Problem, The Dark Forest goes way more out there. First it deals with the immediate aftermath of how society would react to preparing for a space invasion, and then it goes hundreds of years later with even more intense ideas.<br/><br/>I am, however disheartened (no spoilers!), looking forward to reading the third in the trilogy...<br/><br/>Incidentally, an interesting coincidenc</span>
  <span id="freeText15706770075096526421" style="display:none">An incredibly epic science fiction novel! Highly recommended. The scope is amazing. <br /><br />A different style from the more 'grounded' Three Body Problem, The Dark Forest goes way more out there. First it deals with the immediate aftermath of how society would react to preparing for a space invasion, and then it goes hundreds of years later with even more intense ideas.<br /><br />I am, however disheartened (no spoilers!), looking forward to reading the third in the trilogy...<br /><br />Incidentally, an interesting coincidence that I recently read Seveneves by Neal Stephenson which dealt with similar society-dealing-with-the-end-of-the-world themes. Albeit in different ways. Stephenson imagined a deadline of two years and modern technology dealing with it, while Liu gives humanity four hundred years and can be a bit more imaginative. Both give the reader much to think about in these trying times.</span>

<div id="review_1540591420" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1540591420" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7022024-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470679918p2/7022024.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1540591420?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/7022024-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=far-east">far-east</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=science">science</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=here-be-aliens">here-be-aliens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=translated">translated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1540591420" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6562852021636345266">One of the things I found most compelling about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1532777152?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Three Body Problem</a> was the mystery of just what was going on with the science and scientists of Earth. The eventual reveal at the end of the book was quite satisfying but left 'The Dark Forest' in a bit of a bind. Now the reader knew what was going on (<a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[aliens were planning an invasion on Earth and had sent some very troublesome particles to causes problems on Earth <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>) what would drive the story forward?<br/><br/>I think this </span>
  <span id="freeText6562852021636345266" style="display:none">One of the things I found most compelling about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1532777152?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Three Body Problem</a> was the mystery of just what was going on with the science and scientists of Earth. The eventual reveal at the end of the book was quite satisfying but left 'The Dark Forest' in a bit of a bind. Now the reader knew what was going on (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[aliens were planning an invasion on Earth and had sent some very troublesome particles to causes problems on Earth <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>) what would drive the story forward?<br /><br />I think this was where 'The Dark Forest' stumbled. As fascinating as the mystery in 'The Three Body Problem' was, it did mask some of the structural weaknesses of the book. Namely the negligence shown towards character development in favor of advancing the story. I found <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1255491211?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Grace of Kings</a>, another story written in a more traditional Chinese style, to suffer from the same shortcoming. In 'The Dark Forest' I didn't get the sense that the characters had much depth (and don't hold your breathe for a consequential female character). The characters were there to rely information to the reader and advance the story. I didn't feel much for their triumphs or losses and this resulted in a bit of distance between my self and humanity in the book.<br /><br />That weakness aside I did think there were some excellent ideas and execution int his book. For instance, the title of this book ties into a <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[theory of cosmic civilizations. Effectively, the best way to survive in the dark forest of the universe was to do everything you could to not draw attention to your solar system lest another alien civilization discovers you and, through the cold logic of game theory, sets out to destroy you. And this isn't something that is totally absurd, even the great <a href="http://www.space.com/29999-stephen-hawking-intelligent-alien-life-danger.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Stephen Hawking is wary of making ourselves known to alien civilizations</a>. This is all explained in a way that is both simple, enlightening, and very compelling.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Another well done part of this book was the extrapolation of new technologies and their impact on human society. For instance, in the future the degree of connectivity is amped up to 11. Everything is an inter-actable surface. Chairs, tables, clothes, and walls can all connect to the wider net and display information. One interesting consequence of this was the spaceships in the future did not have dedicated spaces. A captain could link into any surface and control the entire ship. This resulted in very generic ship interiors since there is no need for specialized spaces.<br /><br />Future society has also evolved to the point where the space fleets have effectively becomes independent nations with the nations of earth mostly just concerned with keeping order and society operating without worrying about space and those matters. There are no longer competing earth nations and things are generally pretty harmonious while the fleets are united in a common purpose. Human conflict was at an all time low with everyone minding their own respective business.<br /><br />I found the future to be both reasonable and utterly alien. <br /><br />So the good and the bad sort of balance out, it really depends what you like more in your science fiction. The ideas were great and the execution of them wonderful while the characters seemed to be more after thoughts. In a way this reminded me of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Age_of_Science_Fiction" rel="nofollow noopener">Golden Age of Science Fiction</a> in that regard (big ideas, little character), but this is the 21st century and there is no excuse of the negligence of characters this book demonstrated. At the end of the day this was an enjoyable read but it was rather clinical and lacked any emotional punch.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6562852021636345266" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3355175548" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7454524290036815739"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1594288882ra/29785093.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>I wish I liked this book. I really wish I did. It would say more positive things about my intellectual capacities. This is definitely not a book for everyone. If you expect a sci-fi novel, you will be disappointed. If you want to read this book, do it knowing that any expectations you have on it will be proven wrong. This is in some way a good thing, and I experienced this sensation in a positive way while reading the first one. The fact that the first book felt more like a study in philosophy,</span>
  <span id="freeText7454524290036815739" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1594288882ra/29785093.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I wish I liked this book. I really wish I did. It would say more positive things about my intellectual capacities. This is definitely not a book for everyone. If you expect a sci-fi novel, you will be disappointed. If you want to read this book, do it knowing that any expectations you have on it will be proven wrong. This is in some way a good thing, and I experienced this sensation in a positive way while reading the first one. The fact that the first book felt more like a study in philosophy, sociology, history etc. than a novel, felt good in that first one because it was well-balanced with the incredibly imaginative sci-fi element. In this second one, it really feel gratuitous in some parts. And I am not saying this is not masterfully written, it is, just like the first one. Just maybe I wanted it to be a little less boring and a little more fantastic. As always, the idea, the analysis, the competence of the author are masterful; but the result is not as entertaining as it should be, at least if you consider this a "leisure reading". I wished so much to like this book, but the truth is it took me ages to finish it and now I am late for my monthly TBR ahah! It was worth it though! I am glad I didn't DNF it, but I am 90% sure I won't go on with the series.</span>

<div id="review_1230320663" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1230320663" />
    <a title="Zhao Alex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36847811-zhao-alex"><img alt="Zhao Alex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415751629p2/36847811.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1230320663?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zhao Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zhao Alex" href="/user/show/36847811-zhao-alex">Zhao Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1230320663" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1720006087037447070">Structure balance is still a big problem in this book. Characters are better then the previous book, but still not good enough. Liu is not good at characters.<br/><br/>Beside these problems, this book is just absolutely fascinate.<br/><br/>Although I don't fully agree with primary theory in this book, I have to admit it is very well thought and made of pure imagination, philosophy and wisdom. And Liu has obtained amazing achievement on using the theory to create a story that full of suspense, surprise and conflict.</span>
  <span id="freeText1720006087037447070" style="display:none">Structure balance is still a big problem in this book. Characters are better then the previous book, but still not good enough. Liu is not good at characters.<br /><br />Beside these problems, this book is just absolutely fascinate.<br /><br />Although I don't fully agree with primary theory in this book, I have to admit it is very well thought and made of pure imagination, philosophy and wisdom. And Liu has obtained amazing achievement on using the theory to create a story that full of suspense, surprise and conflict.<br />There are a lot of amazing fresh ideas that I've never seen in the other SF books. I said "WOW!" in my mind for thousands of times when I read the book at the first time. <br /><br />Don't miss this book. And don't miss the next book as well. The first book is just a prolonged preface for this story, the real story actually starts from this book, and will end with the answer to the ultimate question of the universe in the next book. <br />(it is not "42" :) )</span>
  <a data-text-id="1720006087037447070" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/7FRX9U0BqdCeP4Qj9Jl3xXHfTBX+a1+MSnbr6wUq4UdEZ/ZJoSseeJRBYkspjssNTC7R9vhHzukbOoQjORh1g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nhSpWenqgUO0cJrdc63b1j4r4XkicthBN4gbfY45kgd8tGffGlornRRZYUTQ2YUlHtwnDq5qagSizSrCrslYVA==')})
  }

This original story by Baoshu―published with Liu’s support―envisions the aftermath of the conflict between humanity and the extraterrestrial Trisolarans.\n\nIn the midst of an interstellar war, Yun Tianming found himself on the front lines. Riddled with cancer, he chose to end his life, only to find himself flash frozen and launched into space where the Trisolaran First Fleet awaited. Captured and tortured beyond endurance for decades, Yun eventually succumbed to helping the aliens subjugate humanity in order to save Earth from complete destruction.\n\nGranted a healthy clone body by the Trisolarans, Yun has spent his very long life in exile as a traitor to the human race. Nearing the end of his existence at last, he suddenly receives another reprieve―and another regeneration. A consciousness calling itself The Spirit has recruited him to wage battle against an entity that threatens the existence of the entire universe.       <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/42713958">Quotes from The Dark Forest</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;The universe is a dark forest. Every civilization is an armed hunter stalking through the trees like a ghost, gently pushing aside branches that block the path and trying to tread without sound. Even breathing is done with care. The hunter has to be careful, because everywhere in the forest are stealthy hunters like him. If he finds other life—another hunter, an angel or a demon, a delicate infant or a tottering old man, a fairy or a demigod—there’s only one thing he can do: open fire and eliminate them. In this forest, hell is other people. An eternal threat that any life that exposes its own existence will be swiftly wiped out. This is the picture of cosmic civilization. It’s the explanation for the Fermi Paradox.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
